	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">East–West Schism</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other schisms between the Church of Rome and the Church of Constantinople, see <a href="/wiki/Rome%E2%80%93Constantinople_schism_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Rome–Constantinople schism (disambiguation)">Rome–Constantinople schism (disambiguation)</a>.</div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the Western Schism of 1378–1417, which is sometimes also called the Great Schism, see <a href="/wiki/Western_Schism" title="Western Schism">Western Schism</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Break of communion between Catholic and Eastern Orthodox churches</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><caption class="summary">East–West Schism</caption><tbody><tr><th scope="row">Date</th><td style="text-align: left;">January–July 1054</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Also known as</th><td style="text-align: left;">Great Schism,<br />Schism of 1054</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Type</th><td style="text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/Schism#Christianity" title="Schism">Christian Schism</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Cause</th><td style="text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_%E2%80%93_Roman_Catholic_ecclesiastical_differences" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox – Roman Catholic ecclesiastical differences">Ecclesiastical differences</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Theological_differences_between_the_Catholic_Church_and_the_Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Theological differences between the Catholic Church and the Eastern Orthodox Church">Theological and Liturgical disputes</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Participants</th><td class="attendee" style="text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_IX" title="Pope Leo IX">Pope Leo IX</a> <br /> <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarch</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_Cerularius" title="Michael I Cerularius">Michael I Cerularius</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Outcome</th><td class="description" style="text-align: left;">Permanent split of the two churches into the modern-day <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Churches</a></td></tr></tbody></table>

<a href="/wiki/File:P_christianity.svg" class="image" title="Christian cross"><img alt="Christian cross" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/20px-P_christianity.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="18" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/30px-P_christianity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/40px-P_christianity.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="360" /></a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Portal:Christianity" title="Portal:Christianity">Christianity portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Christianity_sidebar" title="Template:Christianity sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Christianity_sidebar" title="Template talk:Christianity sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Christianity_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>East–West Schism</b>, also called the <b>Great Schism</b> and the <b>Schism of 1054</b>, was the break of <a href="/wiki/Communion_(Christian)" class="mw-redirect" title="Communion (Christian)">communion</a> between what are now the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Catholic Church">Orthodox Catholic Churches</a>, which had lasted until the 11th century.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The Schism was the culmination of theological and political differences between the Christian East and West which had developed over the preceding centuries.
</p><p>A succession of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_%E2%80%93_Roman_Catholic_ecclesiastical_differences" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox – Roman Catholic ecclesiastical differences">ecclesiastical differences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theological_differences_between_the_Catholic_Church_and_the_Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Theological differences between the Catholic Church and the Eastern Orthodox Church">theological disputes</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Greek_East_and_Latin_West" title="Greek East and Latin West">Greek East and Latin West</a> pre-dated the formal rupture that occurred in 1054.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Prominent among these were the issues of the <a href="/wiki/Filioque" title="Filioque">procession of the Holy Spirit</a>, whether <a href="/wiki/Leavening_agent" title="Leavening agent">leavened</a> or <a href="/wiki/Unleavened_bread" title="Unleavened bread">unleavened bread</a> should be used in the <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Eucharist</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Bishop of Rome</a>'s claim to <a href="/wiki/Papal_supremacy" title="Papal supremacy">universal jurisdiction</a>, and the place of the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">See of Constantinople</a> in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Pentarchy" title="Pentarchy">Pentarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1053, the first step was taken in the process which led to formal <a href="/wiki/Schism" title="Schism">schism</a>: the Greek churches in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">southern Italy</a> were forced either to close or to conform to Latin practices.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bury_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bury-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In retaliation, the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_Cerularius" title="Michael I Cerularius">Michael I Cerularius</a> ordered the closure of all Latin churches in <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>. In 1054, the <a href="/wiki/Papal_legate" title="Papal legate">papal legate</a> sent by <a href="/wiki/Leo_IX" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo IX">Leo IX</a> travelled to Constantinople for purposes that included refusing to Cerularius the title of "<a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecumenical Patriarch">Ecumenical Patriarch</a>" and insisting that he recognize the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a>'s claim to be the head of all the churches.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The main purpose of the papal legation was to seek help from the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Emperor">Byzantine Emperor</a> in view of the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_southern_Italy" title="Norman conquest of southern Italy">Norman conquest of southern Italy</a> and to deal with recent attacks by <a href="/wiki/Leo_of_Ohrid" title="Leo of Ohrid">Leo of Ohrid</a> against the use of unleavened bread and other Western customs,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESiecienski2010113_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESiecienski2010113-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> attacks that had the support of Cerularius. Historian Axel Bayer says the legation was sent in response to two letters, one from the Emperor seeking assistance in arranging a common military campaign by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">western empires</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Normans</a>, and the other from Cerularius.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> On the refusal of Cerularius to accept the demand, the leader of the legation, <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Humbertus" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal Humbertus">Cardinal Humbert of Silva Candida</a>, <a href="/wiki/O.S.B." class="mw-redirect" title="O.S.B.">O.S.B.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Excommunication_(Catholic_Church)" title="Excommunication (Catholic Church)">excommunicated</a> him, and in return Cerularius <a href="/wiki/Excommunicated" class="mw-redirect" title="Excommunicated">excommunicated</a> Humbert and the other legates.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This was only the first act in a centuries-long process that eventually became a complete schism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERunciman1955_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERunciman1955-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The validity of the Western legates' act is doubtful, since Pope Leo had died and Cerularius' excommunication applied only to the legates personally.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Still, the Church split along <a href="/wiki/Doctrine" title="Doctrine">doctrinal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">political</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geographical</a> lines, and the fundamental breach has never been healed, with each side sometimes accusing the other of having fallen into <a href="/wiki/Heresy_in_Christianity" title="Heresy in Christianity">heresy</a> and of having initiated the division. The Latin led <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Massacre_of_the_Latins" title="Massacre of the Latins">Massacre of the Latins</a> in 1182, the West's retaliation in the <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Thessalonica_(1185)" title="Sack of Thessalonica (1185)">Sacking of Thessalonica in 1185</a>, the capture and pillaging of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_(1204)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Constantinople (1204)">Constantinople</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a> in 1204, and the imposition of <a href="/wiki/Patriarch#Other_historical_Latin_patriarchates" title="Patriarch">Latin patriarchs</a> made reconciliation more difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Establishing <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin</a> <a href="/wiki/Hierarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Hierarch">hierarchies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Crusader_states" title="Crusader states">Crusader states</a> meant that there were two rival claimants to each of the patriarchal sees of Antioch, Constantinople, and Jerusalem, making the existence of schism clear.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENichols2010281_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENichols2010281-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Several attempts at reconciliation did not bear fruit. In 1965, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">Pope Paul VI</a> and the Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople <a href="/wiki/Athenagoras_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Athenagoras I">Athenagoras I</a> nullified the <a href="/wiki/Anathema" title="Anathema">anathemas</a> of 1054,<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> although this nullification of measures taken against a few individuals was essentially a goodwill gesture and did not constitute any sort of reunion.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Contacts between the two sides continue: every year a delegation from each joins in the other's celebration of its patronal feast, <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul" title="Feast of Saints Peter and Paul">Saints Peter and Paul</a> (29 June) for <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_Saint_Andrew" class="mw-redirect" title="Feast of Saint Andrew">Saint Andrew</a> (30 November) for Constantinople, and there have been a number of visits by the head of each to the other. The efforts of the Ecumenical Patriarchs towards reconciliation with the Catholic Church have often been the target of sharp criticism from some fellow Orthodox.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="History of the East–West Schism">History of the East–West Schism</a></div>

<p>Autocephaly recognized universally <i>de facto, </i>  by some Autocephalous Churches <i>de jure.</i> Canonicity mostly recognized:
</p>
<div class="hlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_in_America" title="Orthodox Church in America">America</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>Partially recognized autocephaly by Constantinople and the Church of Greece. Canonicity mildly recognized:
</p>
<div class="hlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">Ukraine</a></li></ul>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_liturgical_calendar" title="Eastern Orthodox liturgical calendar">Liturgical calendar</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">

</div></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left">Other topics</div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center"><div class="hlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_church_architecture" title="Eastern Orthodox church architecture">Architecture</a></li>
