<a href="/wiki/File:P_christianity.svg" class="image"><img alt="P christianity.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/30px-P_christianity.svg.png" decoding="async" width="30" height="27" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/45px-P_christianity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/60px-P_christianity.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="360" /></a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Portal:Christianity" title="Portal:Christianity">Christianity portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Historical_Christian_theology" title="Template:Historical Christian theology"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Historical_Christian_theology" title="Template talk:Historical Christian theology"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Historical_Christian_theology&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Jaroslav Pelikan emphasizes that "while the East–West schism stemmed largely from political and ecclesiastical discord, this discord also reflected basic theological differences". Pelikan further argues that the antagonists in the 11th century inappropriately exaggerated their theological differences whereas modern historians tend to minimize them. Pelikan asserts that the documents from that era evidence the "depths of intellectual alienation that had developed between the two sections of Christendom." While the two sides were technically more guilty of schism than heresy, they often charged each other with allegations of heresy. Pelikan describes much of the dispute as dealing with "regional differences in usages and customs" some of which were adiaphorus (i.e. neither right nor wrong). However, he goes on to say that while it was easy in principle to accept the existence of adiaphora, it was difficult in actual practice to distinguish customs which were innocuously adiaphoric from those that had doctrinal implications.<sup id="cite_ref-Pelikan1977_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pelikan1977-231">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecclesiological_disputes">Ecclesiological disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Ecclesiological disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiology" title="Ecclesiology">Ecclesiology</a></div>
<p>Philip Sherrard, an Orthodox theologian asserts that the underlying cause of the East–West schism was and continues to be "the clash of these two fundamentally irreconcilable ecclesiologies." Roger Haight characterizes the question of episcopal authority in the Church as "acute" with the "relative standings of Rome and Constantinople a recurrent source of tension." Haight characterizes the difference in ecclesiologies as "the contrast between a pope with universal jurisdiction and a combination of patriarchal superstructure with an episcopal and synodal communion ecclesiology analogous to that found in <a href="/wiki/Cyprian" title="Cyprian">Cyprian</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Haight2004.p289_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haight2004.p289-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicholas_Afansiev&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nicholas Afansiev (page does not exist)">Nicholas Afansiev</a> has criticized both the Catholic and Orthodox churches for "subscribing to the universal ecclesiology of St. Cyprian of Carthage according to which only one true and universal church can exist."<sup id="cite_ref-DoyleBazzell2012_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DoyleBazzell2012-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_ecclesiologies">Types of ecclesiologies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Types of ecclesiologies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are several different ecclesiologies: "communion ecclesiology", "eucharistic ecclesiology", "baptismal ecclesiology", "trinitarian ecclesiology", "kerygmatic theology".<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Other ecclesiologies are the "hierarchical-institutional" and the "organic-mystical",<sup id="cite_ref-Volf_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volf-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> and the "congregationalist".<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecclesiological_structure">Ecclesiological structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Ecclesiological structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Primacy_of_the_Roman_Pontiff" class="mw-redirect" title="Primacy of the Roman Pontiff">Primacy of the Roman Pontiff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_organization" title="Eastern Orthodox Church organization">Eastern Orthodox Church organization</a></div>
<p>The Eastern Churches maintained the idea that every local city-church with its bishop, presbyters, deacons and people celebrating the <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Eucharist</a> constituted the whole Church. In this view called Eucharistic ecclesiology (or more recently holographic ecclesiology), every bishop is <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a>'s successor in his church ("the Church") and the churches form what <a href="/wiki/Eusebius_of_Caesarea" class="mw-redirect" title="Eusebius of Caesarea">Eusebius</a> called a common union of churches. This implied that all bishops were ontologically equal, although functionally particular bishops could be granted special privileges by other bishops and serve as <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">metropolitans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishops" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishops">archbishops</a> or <a href="/wiki/Patriarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriarchs">patriarchs</a>.
Within the Roman Empire, from the time of Constantine to the final extinction of the empire in 1453, universal ecclesiology, rather than eucharistic, "became the operative principle".<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The view prevailed that, "when the Roman Empire became Christian the perfect world order willed by God had been achieved: one universal empire was sovereign, and coterminous with it was the one universal church".<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Early on, the ecclesiology of the Roman Church was universal in nature, with the idea that the Church was a worldwide organism with a divinely (not functionally) appointed center: the Church/Bishop of Rome.
These two views are still present in modern Eastern Orthodoxy and Catholicism and can be seen as foundational causes for the schisms and Great Schism between East and West.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>"The Orthodox Church does not accept the doctrine of Papal authority set forth in the Vatican Council of 1870, and taught today in the Catholic Church."<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The Orthodox Church has always maintained the original position of <a href="/wiki/Collegiality" title="Collegiality">collegiality</a> of the bishops resulting in the structure of the church being closer to a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The Orthodox have <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">synods</a> where the highest authorities in each Church community are brought together, but, unlike the Catholic Church, no central individual or figure has the absolute and infallible last word on church doctrine. In practice, this has sometimes led to divisions among Greek, Russian, Bulgarian and Ukrainian Orthodox churches, as no central authority can serve as a rallying point for various internal disputes.
</p><p>Early on, the ecclesiology of the Roman Church was universal in nature, with the idea that the Church was a worldwide organism with a divinely (not functionally) appointed center: the Church/Bishop of Rome.
Vatican II re-asserted the importance of collegiality to a degree that appears satisfying to most if not all ecclesial parties.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
Starting from the second half of the 20th century, eucharistic ecclesiology is upheld by Catholic theologians. <a href="/wiki/Henri_de_Lubac" title="Henri de Lubac">Henri de Lubac</a> wrote: "The Church, like the Eucharist, is a mystery of unity – the same mystery, and one with inexhaustible riches. Both are the body of Christ – the same body."<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Ratzinger" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Ratzinger">Joseph Ratzinger</a> called eucharistic ecclesiology "the real core of Vatican II's teaching on the cross".<sup id="cite_ref-Volf_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volf-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> According to Ratzinger, the one church of God exists in no other way than in the various individual local congregations.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> In these the Eucharist is celebrated in union with the Church everywhere.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Eucharistic ecclesiology led Vatican II to "affirm the theological significance of the local church. If each celebration of the Eucharist is a matter not only of Christ's sacramental presence on the altar, but also of his ecclesial presence in the gathered community, then each eucharistic local church must be more than a subset of the universal church; it must be the body of Christ 'in that place'."<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Papal_primacy">Papal primacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Papal primacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The ecclesiological dimension of the East–West schism revolves around the authority of bishops within their dioceses<sup id="cite_ref-Cleenewerck2008.p22_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cleenewerck2008.p22-245">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2012)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the lines of authority between bishops of different dioceses. It is common for Catholics to insist on the primacy of Roman and papal authority based on patristic writings and conciliar documents.<sup id="cite_ref-Shaw2000_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaw2000-246">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Papal_privilege_and_authority">Papal privilege and authority</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Papal privilege and authority">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Pseudo-Isidore" class="mw-redirect" title="Pseudo-Isidore">Pseudo-Isidore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donation_of_Constantine" title="Donation of Constantine">Donation of Constantine</a></div>
<p>The Catholic Church's current official teachings about papal privilege and power that are unacceptable to the Eastern Orthodox churches are the dogma of the <a href="/wiki/Papal_infallibility" title="Papal infallibility">pope's infallibility</a> when speaking officially "from the chair of Peter (ex cathedra Petri)" on matters of faith and morals to be held by the whole Church, so that such definitions are irreformable "of themselves, and not by the consent of the Church" (<i>ex sese et non-ex consensu ecclesiae</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> and have a binding character for all (Catholic) Christians in the world; the pope's direct episcopal jurisdiction over all (Catholic) Christians in the world; the pope's authority to appoint (and so also to depose)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Perhaps (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the bishops of all (Catholic) Christian churches except in the territory of a patriarchate;<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> and the affirmation that the legitimacy and authority of all (Catholic) Christian bishops in the world derive from their union with the Roman see and its bishop, the Supreme Pontiff, the unique Successor of Peter and Vicar of Christ on earth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Perhaps, but http&#58;//www.vatican.va/archive/hist_councils/ii_vatican_council/documents/vat-ii_const_19641121_lumen-gentium_en.html &#39;&#39;Lumen gentium&#39;&#39; says: &#91;The pastoral office or the habitual and daily care of their sheep is entrusted to them (the bishops) completely; nor are they to be regarded as vicars of the Roman Pontiffs, for they exercise an authority that is proper to them, and are quite correctly called &#39;prelates&#39;, heads of the people whom they govern.&#93; (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Principal among the ecclesiastical issues that separate the two churches is the meaning of <a href="/wiki/Papal_primacy" title="Papal primacy">papal primacy</a> within any future unified church. The Orthodox insist that it should be a "primacy of honor", as in the ancient church, and not a "primacy of authority",<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> whereas the Catholics see the pontiff's role as requiring for its exercise power and authority the exact form of which is open to discussion with other Christians.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Orthodox belief, the test of catholicity is adherence to the authority of <i><a href="/wiki/Religious_text#Christianity" title="Religious text">Scripture</a></i> and then by the <i>Holy Tradition</i> of the church. It is not defined by adherence to any particular See. It is the position of the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church</a> that it has never accepted the pope as <i>de jure</i> leader of the entire church. All bishops are equal 'as Peter' therefore every church under every bishop (consecrated in apostolic succession) is fully complete (the original meaning of <i>catholic</i>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Referring to Ignatius of Antioch<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Carlton says
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Contrary to popular opinion, the word catholic does not mean "universal"; it means "whole, complete, lacking nothing." ...Thus, to confess the Church to be catholic is to say that She possesses the fullness of the Christian faith. To say, however, that Orthodox and Rome constitute two lungs of the same Church is to deny that either Church separately is catholic in any meaningful sense of the term. This is not only contrary to the teaching of Orthodoxy, it is flatly contrary to the teaching of the Roman Catholic Church, which considered itself truly catholic<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The church is in the image of the Trinity<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> and reflects the reality of the incarnation.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The body of Christ must always be equal with itself… The local church which manifests the body of Christ cannot be subsumed into any larger organisation or collectivity which makes it more catholic and more in unity, for the simple reason that the principle of total catholicity and total unity is already intrinsic to it.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Any changes to the understanding of the church would reflect a change in the understanding of the Trinity.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theological_issues">Theological issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Theological issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_%E2%80%93_Roman_Catholic_theological_differences" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox – Roman Catholic theological differences">Eastern Orthodox – Roman Catholic theological differences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contra_Errores_Graecorum" title="Contra Errores Graecorum">Contra Errores Graecorum</a></div>
<p>From the perspective of the Catholic Church, the ecclesiological issues are the central issue which is why they characterize the split between the two churches as a schism. In their view, the Eastern Orthodox are very close to them in theology and the Catholic Church does not consider the Orthodox beliefs to be heretical. However, from the perspective of Orthodox theologians, there are theological issues that run much deeper than just the theology around the primacy and/or supremacy of the Pope. In fact, unlike the Catholics, who do not generally consider the Orthodox heretical and speak instead about the Eastern "schism",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFortescue1912_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFortescue1912-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> some prominent Orthodox theologians do consider the Catholic Church to be heretical on fundamental doctrinal issues of theology, such as the <i>Filioque</i>. These issues have a long history as can be seen in the 11th-century works of Orthodox theologian and Saint <a href="/wiki/Nikitas_Stithatos" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikitas Stithatos">Nikitas Stithatos</a>.
</p><p>In the Catholic Church too, some writers can be found who speak <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejoratively</a> of the Eastern Orthodox Church and its theology, but these writers are marginal.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The official view of the Catholic Church is that expressed in the decree <i>Unitatis redintegratio</i> of Vatican II:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In the study of revelation East and West have followed different methods, and have developed differently their understanding and confession of God's truth. It is hardly surprising, then, if from time to time one tradition has come nearer to a full appreciation of some aspects of a mystery of revelation than the other, or has expressed it to better advantage. In such cases, these various theological expressions are to be considered often as mutually complementary rather than conflicting. Where the authentic theological traditions of the Eastern Church are concerned, we must recognize the admirable way in which they have their roots in Holy Scripture, and how they are nurtured and given expression in the life of the liturgy. They derive their strength too from the living tradition of the apostles and from the works of the Fathers and spiritual writers of the Eastern Churches. Thus they promote the right ordering of Christian life and, indeed, pave the way to a full vision of Christian truth.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinity">Trinity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Trinity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Filioque" title="Filioque">Filioque</a></div>
<p>Although the Western churches do not consider the Eastern and Western understanding of the <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinity</a> to be radically different, Eastern theologians such as John S. Romanides and Michael Pomazansky argue that the <i>Filioque</i> clause is symptomatic of a fatal flaw in the Western understanding, which they attribute to the influence of Augustine and, by extension, to that of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Filioque</i>, Latin for "and (from) the Son", was added in <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a> to the Latin text of the <a href="/wiki/Nicene-Constantinopolitan_Creed" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicene-Constantinopolitan Creed">Nicene-Constantinopolitan Creed</a>, which also varies from the original Greek text in having the additional phrase <i>Deum de Deo</i> (God from God)<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schaff_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaff-263">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> and in using the singular "I believe" (Latin, <i>Credo</i>, Greek Πιστεύω) instead of the original "We believe" (Greek Πιστεύομεν),<sup id="cite_ref-Schaff_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaff-263">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> which <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</a> preserves.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Church_of_the_East" title="Assyrian Church of the East">Assyrian Church of the East</a>, which is in communion neither with the Eastern Orthodox Church nor with Oriental Orthodoxy also uses "We believe".<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> <i>Filioque</i> states that the Holy Spirit proceeds from the Son as well as from the Father, a doctrine accepted by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> and by <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant churches</a> in general.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Christians of these groups generally include it when reciting the Nicene Creed. Nonetheless, these groups recognize that <i>Filioque</i> is not part of the original text established at the <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Constantinople" title="First Council of Constantinople">First Council of Constantinople</a> in 381<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> and they do not demand that others too should use it when saying the Creed.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Indeed, the Catholic Church does not add the phrase corresponding to <i>Filioque</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">καὶ τοῦ Υἱοῦ</span>) to the Greek text of the Creed, even in the <a href="/wiki/Liturgy" title="Liturgy">liturgy</a> for <a href="/wiki/Latin_Rite" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin Rite">Latin Rite</a> Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-PCPCU_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCPCU-271">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Council_of_Constantinople_(Eastern_Orthodox)" title="Fourth Council of Constantinople (Eastern Orthodox)">879–880 Council of Constantinople</a> the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> anathematized the "Filioque" phrase, "as a novelty and augmentation of the Creed", and in their 1848 encyclical the Eastern Patriarchs spoke of it as a heresy.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> It was qualified as such by some of the Eastern Orthodox Church's saints, including Photios I of Constantinople, Mark of Ephesus, <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Palamas" title="Gregory Palamas">Gregory Palamas</a>, who have been called the Three Pillars of Orthodoxy.
</p><p>The Eastern church believes by the Western church inserting the Filioque unilaterally (without consulting or holding council with the East) into the Creed that the Western church broke communion with the East.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Orthodox theologians such as <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lossky" title="Vladimir Lossky">Vladimir Lossky</a> criticize the focus of Western theology of God in 'God in uncreated essence' as misguided, which he alleges is a <a href="/wiki/Modalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Modalism">modalistic</a> and therefore a speculative expression of God that is indicative of the <a href="/wiki/Sabellianism" title="Sabellianism">Sabellian</a> heresy.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> Orthodox theologian <a href="/wiki/Michael_Pomazansky" title="Michael Pomazansky">Michael Pomazansky</a> argues that, in order for the Holy Spirit to proceed from the Father and the Son in the Creed, there would have to be two sources in the deity (double procession), whereas in the one God there can only be one source of divinity, which is the Father hypostasis of the Trinity, not God's essence per se.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, Bishop Kallistos Ware suggests that the problem is more in the area of semantics than of basic doctrinal differences.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Experience_of_God_.28Theoria.29_vs._Scholasticism"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Experience_of_God_(Theoria)_vs._Scholasticism">Experience of God (Theoria) vs. Scholasticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Experience of God (Theoria) vs. Scholasticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hesychasm" title="Hesychasm">Hesychasm</a></div>
<p>Lossky, a noted modern <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a> theologian, argues the difference in East and West is due to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>'s use of pagan metaphysical philosophy (and scholasticism) rather than actual experience of God called <i>theoria</i>, to validate the theological dogmas of Catholic Christianity. For this reason, Lossky argues that Eastern Orthodox and Catholics have become "different men".<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Other Eastern Orthodox theologians such as Romanides<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> and Metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Hierotheos_(Vlachos)" title="Hierotheos (Vlachos)">Hierotheos</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nafpaktos" title="Nafpaktos">Nafpaktos</a> have made similar pronouncements.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>
According to the Orthodox teachings, <i>theoria</i> can be achieved through ascetic practices like hesychasm (see St <a href="/wiki/John_Climacus" title="John Climacus">John Climacus</a>), which was condemned as a heresy by <a href="/wiki/Barlaam_of_Seminara" title="Barlaam of Seminara">Barlaam of Seminara</a>.
</p><p>Orthodox theologians charge that, in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox theology">Orthodox theology</a>, western theology is based on philosophical discourse which reduces humanity and nature to cold mechanical concepts.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Orthodox theologians argue that the mind (reason, rationality) is the focus of Western theology, whereas in Eastern theology, the mind must be put in the heart, so they are united into what is called nous, this unity as heart is the focus of Eastern Orthodox Christianity<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> involving the unceasing <a href="/wiki/Prayer_of_the_heart" class="mw-redirect" title="Prayer of the heart">Prayer of the heart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Theological_consequences_of_the_division_East_and_West">Theological consequences of the division East and West</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Theological consequences of the division East and West">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Noesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Noesis">Noesis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_warfare" title="Spiritual warfare">Spiritual warfare</a></div>
<p>In Orthodox theology, in the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Ascetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascetic">ascetic</a> traditions one of the goals of ascetic practice is to obtain sobriety of consciousness, awakeness (<a href="/wiki/Nepsis" title="Nepsis">nepsis</a>). For humankind this is reached in the healing of whole person called the <a href="/wiki/Soul" title="Soul">soul</a>, heart. When a person's heart is reconciled with their mind, this is referred to as a healing of the nous or the "eye, focus of the heart or soul".<sup id="cite_ref-Neptic_Monasticism_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neptic_Monasticism-283">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> Part of this process is the healing and or reconciliation of humankind's <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">reason</a> being called <i>logos</i> or <i>dianoia</i> with the heart, soul.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> While mankind's spirit and body are energies vivified by the soul, Orthodoxy teaches man's sin, suffering, sorrow is caused by his heart and mind being a duality and in conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> According to Orthodox theology, lack of <a href="/wiki/Nous" title="Nous">noetic</a> understanding (sickness) can be neither circumvented nor satisfied by rational or discursive thought (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Systematization" class="mw-redirect" title="Systematization">systematization</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Neptic_Monasticism_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neptic_Monasticism-283">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> and denying the needs of the human heart (a more Western expression would be the needs of the soul) causes various negative or destructive manifestations such as addiction, atheism and evil thoughts etc.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> A cleaned, healed or restored Nous creates the condition of <a href="/wiki/Sobriety" title="Sobriety">sobriety</a> or nepsis of the mind.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Uncreated_light">Uncreated light</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Uncreated light">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kollyvades_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Kollyvades Movement">Kollyvades Movement</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tabor_light" class="mw-redirect" title="Tabor light">Tabor light</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Kabasilas" title="Nicholas Kabasilas">Nicholas Kabasilas</a></div>
<p>Orthodox theologians assert that the theological division of East and West culminated into a direct theological conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/Hesychasm_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="Hesychasm controversy">Hesychasm controversy</a> during several councils at Constantinople New Rome, between the years 1341–1351. They argue that this controversy highlighted the sharp contrast between what is embraced by the Catholic Church as proper (or orthodox) theological dogma and how theology is validated and what is considered valid theology by the Eastern Orthodox. The essence of the disagreement is that in the East a person cannot be a genuine true theologian, or teach knowledge of God, without having experienced God, as is defined as the vision of God (<i>theoria</i>). At the heart of the issue was the teaching of the <a href="/wiki/Essence-Energies_distinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Essence-Energies distinction">Essence-Energies distinctions</a> (which states that while creation can never know God's uncreated essence, it can know his uncreated energies) by Gregory Palamas.
</p>
<h4><span id="Original_sin.2C_free_will_and_the_Immaculate_Conception"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_sin,_free_will_and_the_Immaculate_Conception">Original sin, free will and the Immaculate Conception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Original sin, free will and the Immaculate Conception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span id="Augustine.27s_doctrine_of_original_sin"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Augustine's_doctrine_of_original_sin">Augustine's doctrine of original sin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Augustine&#039;s doctrine of original sin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Traducianism" title="Traducianism">Traducianism</a></div>
<p>The Eastern Orthodox do not accept <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine</a>'s teaching of original sin. His interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Ancestral_sin" title="Ancestral sin">ancestral sin</a> is rejected in the East as well. Nor is Augustine's teaching accepted in its totality in the West.<sup id="cite_ref-Neuro_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuro-289">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> The Catholic Church rejects <a href="/wiki/Traducianism" title="Traducianism">traducianism</a> and affirms <a href="/wiki/Creationism_(soul)" title="Creationism (soul)">creationism</a>. Its teaching on original sin is largely based on but not identical with that of Augustine, and is opposed to the interpretation of Augustine advanced by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>. Its teaching departs from Augustine's ideas in some respects.<sup id="cite_ref-Neuro_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuro-289">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> The Eastern Church makes no use at all of Augustine. Another Orthodox view is expressed by <a href="/wiki/Christos_Yannaras" title="Christos Yannaras">Christos Yannaras</a>, who described Augustine as "the fount of every distortion and alteration in the Church's truth in the West".<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_teachings_on_original_sin">Church teachings on original sin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Church teachings on original sin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>What the Eastern Orthodox accepts is that ancestral sin corrupted their existence (their bodies and environment) that each person is born into and thus we are born into a corrupted existence (by the ancestral sin of Adam and Eve)<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> and that "original sin is hereditary. It did not remain only Adam and Eve's. As life passes from them to all of their descendants, so does original sin. All of us participate in original sin because we are all descended from the same forefather, Adam."<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> And the teaching of the Eastern Orthodox Church is that, as a result of Adam's sin, "hereditary sin flowed to his posterity; so that everyone who is born after the flesh bears this burden, and experiences the fruits of it in this present world."<sup id="cite_ref-Dositheus6_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dositheus6-294">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly, what the Catholic Church holds is that the sin of Adam that we inherit, and for the remission of which even babies who have no personal sin are baptized,<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> is called "sin" only in an analogical sense, since it is not an act committed like the personal sin of Adam and Eve, but a fallen state contracted by the transmission of a human nature deprived of original holiness and justice.<sup id="cite_ref-CCC405_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC405-296">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Both East<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and West<sup id="cite_ref-CCC405_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC405-296">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> hold that each person is not called to atone for the actual sin committed by Adam and Eve. 
</p><p>According to the Western Church, "original sin does not have the character of a personal fault in any of Adam's descendants",<sup id="cite_ref-CCC405_296-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC405-296">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> and the Eastern Church teaches that "by these fruits and this burden we do not understand [actual] sin".<sup id="cite_ref-Dositheus6_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dositheus6-294">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> The Orthodox<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the Catholics<sup id="cite_ref-CCC418_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC418-297">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> believe that people inherit only the spiritual sickness (in which all suffer and sin) of Adam and Eve, caused by their ancestral sin (what has flowed to them), a sickness leaving them weakened in their powers, subject to ignorance, suffering and the domination of death, and inclined to sin.<sup id="cite_ref-CCC418_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC418-297">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Immaculate_Conception_rejected_by_the_East">Immaculate Conception rejected by the East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Immaculate Conception rejected by the East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The Catholic doctrine of the Immaculate Conception, which claims that God protected the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a> from original sin through no merit of her own,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> was dogmatically defined by Pope <a href="/wiki/Pius_IX" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius IX">Pius IX</a> in 1854. Instead, Orthodox theology proclaims that Mary was chosen to bear Christ, having first found favor of God by her purity and obedience.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Sin.2C_Purgatory_and_Hell"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sin,_Purgatory_and_Hell">Sin, Purgatory and Hell</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sin, Purgatory and Hell">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Purgatory">Purgatory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Purgatory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Another point of theological contention between the western and eastern churches is the doctrine of purgatory (as it was shown at the <a href="/wiki/Second_Council_of_Lyons" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Council of Lyons">Second Council of Lyons</a> and the Council of Ferrara–Florence).<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> It was developed in time in western theology, according to which, "all who die in God's grace and friendship, but still imperfectly purified, are indeed assured of their eternal salvation; but after death they undergo purification, so as to achieve the holiness necessary to enter the joy of heaven."<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> However, some eastern theologians, while agreeing that there is beyond death a state in which believers continue to be perfected and led to full divinization, consider that it is a state not of punishment but of growth;<sup id="cite_ref-Confessions_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Confessions-308">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> hold that suffering cannot purify sin, since they have a different view of sin and consider suffering as a result of a spiritual sickness.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> Western theology usually considers sin not only as a sickness that weakens and impedes, but also as something that merits punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Eastern Orthodox Church holds that "there is a state beyond death where believers continue to be perfected and led to full divinization".<sup id="cite_ref-Confessions_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Confessions-308">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="please find an orthodox source (June 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Although some Orthodox<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2010)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> have described this intermediate state as <i>purgatory</i>, others distinguish it from aspects associated with it in the West: at the Council of Ferrara–Florence, the Orthodox Bishop Mark of Ephesus argued that there are in it no purifying fires.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Damnation">Damnation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Damnation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The traditional Orthodox teaching is that "those who reject Christ will face punishment. According to the Confession of Dositheus, persons go immediately to joy in Christ or to the torments of punishment".<sup id="cite_ref-Confessions_308-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Confessions-308">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Orthodox doctrine there is no place without God. In eternity there is no hiding from God. In Catholic theology, God is present everywhere not only by his power but in himself.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> Hell is a state of self-selected separation from God.
</p><p>Eastern theology considers the desire to sin to be the result of a spiritual sickness (caused by Adam and Eve's pride), which needs to be cured.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> One such theologian gives his interpretation of Western theology as follows: "According to the holy Fathers of the Church, there is not an uncreated Paradise and a created Hell, as the Franco–Latin tradition teaches".<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> The eastern Church believes that hell or eternal damnation and heaven exist and are the same place, which is being with God, and that the very same divine love (God's uncreated energies) which is a source of bliss and consolation for the righteous (because they love God, His love is heaven for them) is also a source of torment (or a "Lake of Fire") for sinners (because they don't love God, they will feel His love this way).<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> The Western Church speaks of heaven<sup id="cite_ref-CCC1024_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC1024-319">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> and hell<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> as states of existence rather than as places, while in Eastern Orthodoxy there is no hell per se, there is damnation or punishment in eternity for the rejection of God's grace.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">

</li>
<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Following the establishment of Constantinople (the ancient city of Byzantium) as the state capital of the Roman Empire in the early part of the 4th century, a series of significant ecclesiastical events saw the status of the Bishop of <a href="/wiki/New_Rome" title="New Rome">New Rome</a> (as Constantinople was then called) elevated to its current position and privilege.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></span>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-154"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-154">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"&#91;...&#93; the Roman legates excommunicated him &#91;...&#93; But &#91;...&#93; there was no &#91;...&#93; general excommunication of the Byzantine Church, still less of all the East. The legates carefully provided against that in their Bull. &#91;...&#93; They excommunicated Caerularius, Leo of Achrida, and their adherents. &#91;...&#93; The real tragedy is that gradually all the other Eastern patriarchs took sides with Caerularius, &#91;...&#93; and chose &#91;...&#93; to share his schism. &#91;...&#93; The emperor (not <a href="/wiki/Constantine_IX_Monomachos" title="Constantine IX Monomachos">Constantine IX</a>, but his successor) was on the side of his patriarch and they had learned too well to consider the emperor as their over-lord in spiritual matters too. &#91;...&#93; it was the usurped authority of Constantinople, the Erastianism of the East that turned a personal quarrel into a great schism."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFortescue1912_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFortescue1912-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></span>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East%E2%80%93West_Schism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation">"Great Schism", <i>Oxford Dictionary of the Christian <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The absence of full communion between the churches is mentioned explicitly even in the permission that <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.intratext.com/IXT/ENG0017/_P2S.HTM">canon 844 §3 of the Code of Canon Law</a> accords for the administering by Catholic ministers of the sacraments of penance, the Eucharist and anointing of the sick to spontaneously requesting members of eastern churches such as the Eastern Orthodox Church (as also the <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a> churches and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_East" title="Church of the East">Church of the East</a>) and of western churches such as the Old Catholic Church.</span>

<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFBakerLanders2005" class="citation">Baker, Robert Andrew; Landers, John M (2005), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=MQvCL1STfaAC&amp;pg=PA110"><i>A Summary of Christian History</i></a>, B&amp;H, p.&#160;110, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-80543288-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-80543288-6"><bdi>978-0-80543288-6</bdi></a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Summary+of+Christian+History&amp;rft.pages=110&amp;rft.pub=B%26H&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-80543288-6&amp;rft.aulast=Baker&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert+Andrew&amp;rft.au=Landers%2C+John+M&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DMQvCL1STfaAC%26pg%3DPA110&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.oca.org/FSLivesAllSaints.asp?SID=4&amp;M=6&amp;D=4"><i>St Metrophanes the first Patriarch of Constantinople</i></a>, OCA, <q>Saint Metrophanes, Patriarch of Constantinople, was a contemporary of St Constantine the Great (306–337). His father, Dometius, was a brother of the Roman emperor Probus (276–282). Seeing the falseness of the pagan religion, Dometius came to believe in Christ. During a time of terrible persecution of Christians at Rome, St Dometius set off to Byzantium with two of his sons, Probus and Metrophanes. They were instructed in the law of the Lord by Bishop Titus, a man of holy life. Seeing the ardent desire of Dometius to labor for the Lord, St Titus ordained him presbyter. After the death of Titus first Dometius (272–303) was elevated to the bishop's throne, and thereafter his sons, Probus (303–315) and in 316 St Metrophanes. The emperor Constantine once came to Byzantium, and was delighted by the beauty and comfortable setting of the city. And having seen the holiness of life and sagacity of St Metrophanes, the emperor took him back to Rome. Soon Constantine the Great transferred the capital from Rome to Byzantium and he brought St Metrophanes there. The First Ecumenical Council was convened in 325 to resolve the Arian heresy. Constantine the Great had the holy Fathers of the Council bestow upon St Metrophanes the title of Patriarch. Thus, the saint became the first Patriarch of Constantinople.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=St+Metrophanes+the+first+Patriarch+of+Constantinople&amp;rft.pub=OCA&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.oca.org%2FFSLivesAllSaints.asp%3FSID%3D4%26M%3D6%26D%3D4&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100510123826/http://www.patriarchate.org/patriarchate/history"><i>History</i></a>, The Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.patriarchate.org/patriarchate/history">the original</a> on 10 May 2010, <q>Following the establishment of Constantinople (the ancient city of Byzantium) as the state capital of the Roman Empire in the early part of the fourth century, a series of significant ecclesiastical events saw the status of the Bishop of New Rome (as Constantinople was then called) elevated to its current position and privilege</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=History&amp;rft.pub=The+Ecumenical+Patriarchate+of+Constantinople&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.patriarchate.org%2Fpatriarchate%2Fhistory&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-ReferenceB-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ReferenceB_61-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ReferenceB_61-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFSchaff2005" class="citation">Schaff, Philip, ed. (1 June 2005), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ccel.org/ccel/schaff/npnf214.xi.xviii.xxviii.html"><i>The Seven Ecumenical Councils</i></a>, The Christian Classics Ethereal Library, NPNF2-14<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 June</span> 2012</span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Seven+Ecumenical+Councils&amp;rft.pages=NPNF2-14&amp;rft.pub=The+Christian+Classics+Ethereal+Library&amp;rft.date=2005-06-01&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ccel.org%2Fccel%2Fschaff%2Fnpnf214.xi.xviii.xxviii.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFRomanides" class="citation">Romanides, John, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.romanity.org/htm/rom.16.en.romanity_romania_roumeli.01.htm"><i>Romanity</i></a>, <q>There are no primacies nor primates according to Roman Orthodox Canon Law, but only bishops with "Seniority of Honor" since all bishops are doctrinally equal. The Franco-Latin and Protestant translations of "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Seniority_of_honor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Seniority of honor (page does not exist)">Seniority of honor</a>" by "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Primacy_of_honor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Primacy of honor (page does not exist)">primacy of honor</a>" is theirs, not ours</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Romanity&amp;rft.aulast=Romanides&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.romanity.org%2Fhtm%2From.16.en.romanity_romania_roumeli.01.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ccel.org/ccel/schaff/npnf214.xi.xviii.xxviii.html">"Canon XXVIII"</a>. Fourth Ecumenical Council. <q>[T]he Fathers rightly granted privileges to the throne of old Rome, because it was the royal city. And the One Hundred and Fifty most religious Bishops [i.e., the Second Ecumenical Council], actuated by the same consideration, gave equal privileges (ἴσα πρεσβεῖα) to the most holy throne of New Rome, justly judging that the city which is honored with the Sovereignty and the Senate, and enjoys equal privileges with the old imperial Rome, should in ecclesiastical matters also be magnified as she is, and rank next after her; so that, in the Pontic, the Asian, and the Thracian dioceses, the metropolitans only and such bishops also of the Dioceses aforesaid as are among the barbarians, should be ordained by the aforesaid most holy throne of the most holy Church of Constantinople.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Canon+XXVIII&amp;rft.pub=Fourth+Ecumenical+Council&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ccel.org%2Fccel%2Fschaff%2Fnpnf214.xi.xviii.xxviii.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Hartmann, Wilfried; Pennington, Kenneth (2012). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=BwnCVYHf5VAC&amp;pg=PA63"><i>The History of Byzantine and Eastern Canon Law to 1500</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.newadvent.org/fathers/3810.htm">Extracts from the Acts of the Council of Ephesus</a>). The creed quoted in the Acts of the Council of Ephesus (the Third Ecumenical Council) is that of the first Ecumenical Council, not the creed as modified by the second Ecumenical Council, and so does not have additions such as "who proceeds from the Father" (<i>ibidem</i>).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ccel.org/ccel/schaff/npnf214.ix.i.html">NPNF2-14. The Seven Ecumenical Councils – Christian Classics Ethereal Library</a>. Ccel.org (1 June 2005). Retrieved 2 June 2012.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ccel.org/ccel/schaff/npnf214.x.xvi.x.html">seventh canon of the Council of Ephesus</a> declared: "It is unlawful for any man to bring forward, or to write, or to compose a different (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">ἑτέραν</span>) Faith as a rival to that established by the holy Fathers assembled with the Holy Ghost in Nicæa. But those who shall dare to compose a different faith, or to introduce or offer it to persons desiring to turn to the acknowledgment of the truth, whether from Heathenism or from Judaism, or from any heresy whatsoever, shall be deposed, if they be bishops or clergymen; bishops from the episcopate and clergymen from the clergy; and if they be laymen, they shall be <a href="/wiki/Anathematized" class="mw-redirect" title="Anathematized">anathematized</a>."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Excursus-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Excursus_112-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Excursus_112-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ccel.org/ccel/schaff/npnf214.x.xvi.xi.html">"Excursus on the words πίστιν ἑτέραν"</a>. <li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.monachos.net/content/patristics/patristictexts/34-patrtexts/152-ephesus-definition-nicaea">Council of Ephesus, 431: Definition of the faith at Nicaea</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120418215517/http://www.monachos.net/content/patristics/patristictexts/34-patrtexts/152-ephesus-definition-nicaea">Archived</a> 18 April 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span>

<li id="cite_note-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-115">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"However, the chief of the heretics who distorted the apostolic teaching concerning the Holy Spirit was Macedonius, who occupied the cathedra of Constantinople as archbishop in the 4th century and found followers for himself among former Arians and Semi-Arians. He called the Holy Spirit a creation of the Son, and a servant of the Father and the Son. Accusers of his heresy were Fathers of the Church like Sts. Basil the Great, Gregory the Theologian, Athanasius the Great, Gregory of Nyssa, Ambrose, Amphilocius, Diodores of Tarsus, and others, who wrote works against the heretics. The false teaching of Macedonius was refuted first in a series of local councils and finally at the Second Ecumenical Council of Constantinople in 381. In preserving Orthodoxy, the Second Ecumenical Council completed the Nicaean Symbol of Faith with these words: "And in the Holy Spirit, the Lord, the Giver of Life, Who proceedeth from the Father, Who with the Father and the Son is equally worshiped and glorified, Who spake by the Prophets," as well as those articles of the Creed which follow this in the Nicaean-Constantinopolitan Symbol of Faith." Orthodox Dogmatic Theology: A Concise Exposition Protopresbyter <a href="/wiki/Michael_Pomazansky" title="Michael Pomazansky">Michael Pomazansky</a> St Herman of Alaska Brotherhood press 1994 (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-938635-69-7" title="Special:BookSources/0-938635-69-7">0-938635-69-7</a>) <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.intratext.com/IXT/ENG0824/_P17.HTM">[1]</a></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Orthodox attitude to the papacy is expressed by a 12th-century writer, <a href="/wiki/Nicetas_of_Nicomedia" title="Nicetas of Nicomedia">Nicetas</a>, Archbishop of Nicomedia

<dl><dd>My dearest brother, we do not deny to the Roman Church the primacy amongst the five sister Patriarchates; and we recognize her right to the most honorable seat at an Ecumenical Council. But she has separated herself from us by her own deeds, when through pride she assumed a monarchy which does not belong to her office... How shall we accept decrees from her that have been issued without consulting us and even without our knowledge? If the Roman Pontiff, seated on the lofty throne of his glory, wishes to thunder at us and, so to speak, hurl his mandates at us from on high, and if he wishes to judge us and even to rule us and our Churches, not by taking counsel with us but at his own arbitrary pleasure, what kind of brotherhood, or even what kind of parenthood can this be? We should be the slaves, not the sons, of such a Church, and the Roman See would not be the pious mother of sons but a hard and imperious mistress of slaves (Quoted in S. Runciman, The Eastern Schism, p. 116). Orthodox Church by Bishop <a href="/wiki/Kallistos_Ware" title="Kallistos Ware">Kallistos Ware</a> Part I: History. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-14-014656-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-14-014656-1">978-0-14-014656-1</a>.</dd></dl>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation">"Eighth Ecumenical Council: Constantinople IV (869)", <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.newadvent.org/cathen/04423f.htm"><i>The Catholic encyclopædia</i></a>, New advent, <q>The Fourth General Council of Constantinople, under Pope Adrian II and Emperor Basil numbering 102 bishops, 3 papal legates, and 4 patriarchs, consigned to the flames the Acts of an irregular council (conciliabulum) brought together by Photius against Pope Nicholas and Ignatius the legitimate Patriarch of Constantinople; it condemned Photius who had unlawfully seized the patriarchal dignity. The Photian Schism, however, triumphed in the Greek Church, and no other general council took place in the East</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Eighth+Ecumenical+Council%3A+Constantinople+IV+%28869%29&amp;rft.btitle=The+Catholic+encyclop%C3%A6dia&amp;rft.pub=New+advent&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.newadvent.org%2Fcathen%2F04423f.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Cambridge-161"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cambridge_161-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1IhKYifENTMC"><i>The Cambridge Illustrated History of the Middle Ages: 950–1250</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-162">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">J. Harris, <i>Byzantium and the Crusades</i>, 112</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-ccel.org-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ccel.org_163-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ccel.org_163-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">During the Crusades the schism was deepened by the brutal atrocities of the French and Venetian soldiers in the pillage of Constantinople (1204), the establishment of a Latin empire, and the appointment by the pope of Latin bishops in Greek sees.318 Although this artificial empire lasted only half a century (1204–1261), it left a legacy of burning hatred in the memories of horrible desecrations and innumerable insults and outrages, which the East had to endure from the Western barbarians. Churches and monasteries were robbed and desecrated, the Greek service mocked, the clergy persecuted, and every law of decency set at defiance. In Constantinople "a prostitute was seated on the throne of the patriarch; and that daughter of Belial, as she is styled, sung and danced in the church to ridicule the hymns and processions of the Orientals." Even Pope Innocent III accuses the pilgrims that they spared in their lust neither age nor sex, nor religious profession, and that they committed fornication, adultery, and incest in open day (in oculis omnium), "abandoning matrons and virgins dedicated to God to the lewdness of grooms." And yet this great pope insulted the Eastern church by the establishment of a Latin hierarchy on the ruins of the Byzantine empire.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.ccel.org/s/schaff/history/4_ch05.htm">[2]</a></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-officialview-193"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-officialview_193-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://mospat.ru/ru/2010/02/16/news13315/"><bdi lang="ru">Современное состояние отношений между Русской Православной и Римско-Католической Церквами: официальный взгляд, Алексей Дикарев</bdi></a> (in Russian). The official web site of the Moscow Patriarchate. 16 February 2010. <q>К сожалению, двусторонние отношения между нашими Церквами на российской и вообще постсоветской территории трудно назвать нормальными. Здесь ситуация является, пожалуй, наиболее сложной. Московский Патриархат продолжает выражать свою озабоченность политикой Греко-Католической Церкви на Украине и отдельными случаями католического прозелитизма в России. Несомненно, современная ситуация больше не является столь критичной, как еще 10 лет назад, и конфликт перестал носить столь острый характер. Однако до сих пор вышеуказанные проблемы не нашли удовлетворительного решения. Даже если между православными и греко-католиками на Украине больше не происходит кровавых столкновений, характерных для начала 90-х г.г., тем не менее конфликт продолжает оставаться неурегулированным. На Западной Украине православные, большинство которых принадлежит к Московскому Патриархату, ощущают себя ущемляемым в правах меньшинством.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B5+%D1%81%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5+%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9+%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D1%83+%D0%A0%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9+%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9+%D0%B8+%D0%A0%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9+%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%3A+%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9+%D0%B2%D0%B7%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%8F%D0%B4%2C+%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9+%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B2&amp;rft.date=2010-02-16&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fmospat.ru%2Fru%2F2010%2F02%2F16%2Fnews13315%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast%E2%80%93West+Schism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-VIS2016-197"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-VIS2016_197-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160213144411/http://visnews-en.blogspot.com/2016/02/historic-encounter-between-pope-and.html">"Historic encounter between the Pope and Patriarch of Moscow and All Russia: Orthodox and Catholics are brothers, not competitors"</a>. <i>visnews-en.blogspot.com</i>.
